The new system features newly developed magenta and black inks that &#8220;contribute to an expanded color gamut for reds and blues and more faithful reproduction of blacks while also improving black densities.&#8221;</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/frontview-800x326.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"326\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465851\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/closedview-800x349.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"349\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465852\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/topview-800x523.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"523\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465853\" /></p>\n<p>The printer also features improved media capabilities, including &#8220;the ability for professional photographers to print on a range of photo paper surfaces and finishes up to 0.6mm thickness in addition to producing panorama size prints and gallery wrap support functions.&#8221;</p>\n<p>A standard high-grade A3+ bordered color print can be completed in about 1 minute 30 seconds.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/openview-800x549.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"549\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465850\" /></p>\n<p>Other features and specs of the PIXMA PRO-200 include 3 connectivity methods (Wi-Fi, Ethernet, USB), a 3-inch LCD display, a compact design (footprint of 25.1x15x7.9in/639Ã—379Ã—200mm), a skew correction function (to prevent misalignment), and a maximum print resolution of 4800x2400dpi.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/wifiprinting-800x549.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"549\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465854\" /></p>\n<p>Pricing and availability have yet to be announced by Canon Australia. continent. Why? According to Canon, they want to &#8220;support local retail partners&#8221; by sending customers their way.</p>\n<p>The announcement was published on September 1st, and it&#8217;s a notice of sorts: on September 30th, the Canon Australia online store will shut down &#8220;for the foreseeable future.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;The unprecedented challenges currently facing the Australian market has seen Canon Australia re-examine the best way to help consumers access our products, services and support,&#8221; writes Canon. &#8220;As a result, we are proudly streamlining our efforts in supporting local retailers to drive competition in the local market and bring you the best value product offers, promotions, services and experiences possible.&#8221;</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465831\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465831\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/canonstore-800x610.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"610\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465831\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465831\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Many items are already marked &#8220;Out of Stock&#8221; on the online store as of this writing.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Customers can still order products from the Canon Australia online store from now until September 30th, and they will still receive free shipping and Canon&#8217;s &#8220;14 Day Peace of Mind return policy.&#8221; After thatâ€”or if you&#8217;re looking at a product that&#8217;s on backorderâ€”you&#8217;ll need to order from one of Canon&#8217;s official retail partners. If you have a gift card or voucher for the Canon Store, you&#8217;ll need to either use it by September 30th or get in touch with Canon to see how you can carry over those funds.</p>\n<p>The cynical among us will wonder if this has more to do with cutting costs than &#8220;supporting retail partners,&#8221; but whatever the reason, it seems Canon AU is doing its best to make this a streamlined process for everyone. </p>\n<p>We&#8217;ll be keeping a close eye on this development moving forward, just in case Canon is planning to roll out this strategy to other regions like Europe and North America. src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/luminarai_feat-800x420.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"420\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465795\" /></p>\n<p>Skylum has announced a new, AI-first version of its Lumiar photo editor. Dubbed <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fskylum.com%2Fluminar-ai\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Luminar AI</a>, the program takes all of the machine-learning tools from Luminar 4, adds some more, and puts them all into a new app and plugin that&#8217;s all about &#8220;reinventing&#8221; traditional photo editing.</p>\n<p>Skylum has been adding AI-powered features to its more &#8220;traditional&#8221; Luminar photo editor for years now, but Luminar AI takes that sort of automation a big step forward by building the entire experience around AI instead of the regular editing tools that we all know so well. </p>\n<p>When you import a photo into Luminar AI you won&#8217;t see sliders for Brightness or Contrast, or a Curves adjustment, or a Healing brush. Instead, you&#8217;ll see sections like Portrait and Essentials, each of which is made up of different AI tools like BodyAI, FaceAI, and IrisAI for portraits, AtmosphereAI, SkyAI, and Sunrays for landscape editing, and more general tools like CompositionAI and StructureAI to change the overall look of an image.</p>\n<p><div class=\"fluid-iframe\" style=\"max-width: 800px;\"><div class=\"fluid-iframe__inner\" style=\"padding-top:56.25%\"><iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/yJ6_Sz2bmw0\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></div></div></p>\n<p>To be clear, those more traditional tools are still there, probably hiding under the &#8220;PRO&#8221; tab you see in the screenshots below. We asked Luminar about this and they said that they&#8217;re &#8220;keeping most of the traditional editing tools.&#8221; Luminar AI just puts a heavy emphasis on using the aforementioned AI tools and the program&#8217;s built-in AI templates <em>first</em>, in the hopes that you&#8217;ll never have to fiddle with sliders again.</p>\n<p>â€œLuminar AI will help make image editing easier for everyone. Weâ€™ve removed the boring and difficult parts of photo editing without sacrificing creativity,&#8221; says Skylum CEO Alex Tsepko. &#8220;Luminar AI will be a great tool in a creatorâ€™s workflow. They can focus on great results â€” not on the process of editing.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Today&#8217;s announcement is sort of a &#8220;first step&#8221; sneak peek, with more details to be revealed in the next few months ahead of release. For now, everything we know is contained on <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fskylum.com%2Fluminar-ai\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">this website</a> and in the screenshots included below:</p>\n<p><img available as a stand-alone application or as a plug-in for both macOS and Windows sometime &#8220;this holiday season.&#8221; For now, interested photographers can pre-order it at a special early bird price (limited to 30,000 orders) of $60 for current Skylum product owners or $70 for new customers. </p>\n<p>Note that if you <em>do</em> manage to snag that early bird deal, you&#8217;ll get access to the app earlier than the rest of the world, and will also be invited to join the Luminar AI Insider program&#8230; whatever that is.</p>\n<p>To learn more or reserve a copy for yourself, head over style=\"max-width: 800px;\"><div class=\"fluid-iframe__inner\" style=\"padding-top:56.25%\"><iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/nr-F9_4tvjQ\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></div></div></p>\n<p>Photographer <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.patrickhall.photography%2F\" href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Ffstoppers.com%2Fapps%2Fwill-camera-flash-make-iphone-professional-camera-514314\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\"><em>Fstoppers</em></a> recently put Profoto&#8217;s &#8216;AirX&#8217; iPhone flash sync technology to the test. Using just an iPhone and a Profoto B10, he set out to find out if professional off-camera flash is the &#8220;future&#8221; of iPhone photography. </p>\n<p>For those who aren&#8217;t familiar, Profoto unveiled its Air X technology <a href=\"https://petapixel.com/2020/07/08/you-can-now-use-profotos-b10-studio-strobes-with-your-smartphone/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\">back in July</a>, calling it &#8220;an innovation that rewrites the rules of photography.&#8221; That&#8217;s because Air X allows you to sync an iPhone with a professional-grade <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.adorama.com%2Fpp901163.html\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Profoto B10</a> or <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.adorama.com%2Fpp901164.html\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">B10 Plus</a> monolight at speeds up to 1/25,000sâ€”something that simply wasn&#8217;t possible before.</p>\n<p>Still, what works on paper doesn&#8217;t always translate to real life, and so Hall decided to update his own Profoto B10 and put the technology to the test in a real life portrait shoot using an iPhone as his main camera. That&#8217;s what he does in the video above, and the results&#8230; well&#8230; they&#8217;re pretty impressive.</p>\n<p>This is what the system looks like when you&#8217;re actually shooting:</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/fstoppers_how_to_photograph_bridal_portraits_on_iphone_phone.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"510\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-465640\" /></p>\n<p>And these are the kinds of photos that Hall was able to capture using the combination:</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/sample1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"525\" height=\"714\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-465714\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/sample2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"411\" height=\"533\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465715\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/sample3.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"631\" height=\"533\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465716\" /></p>\n<p>For the sake of comparison, Patrick also shot some side-by-side images that show the difference that the off-camera flash can actually make.</p>\n<p>On the left is an image captured using only natural light and exposing for the background; in the middle is an image captured using only natural light and exposing for the subject; and on the right is the same scene captured using the off-camera flash to balance the light. If anything, the final image is a little over-exposed, which allowed Hall to drop the flash power in order to capture the final image from that scene.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/1-800x326.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"326\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465642\" /></p>\n<p>Despite his initial skepticism, Hall was definitely impressed by how well the B10 + iPhone combo performed. For now, the tech is still limited to the (relatively expensive) <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.adorama.com%2Fpp901163.html%3Fkbid%3D67085\" rel=\"norewrite follow external noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Profoto B10</a>, but if and when this syncing technology expands to other flash heads, other brands, and Android phones, we may see a big spike in the quality of smartphone photography that professionals are able to capture.</p>\n<p>To dive deeper into this comparison and see more sample shots for yourself, check out the full video up top or head over to Fstoppers and read <a +0000","feedId":607,"bgimg":"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/fstoppers_how_to_photograph_bridal_portraits_on_iphone_phone.jpg","linkMd5":"5a4b470409bbb773da7e2d6688c2a9aa","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn57@2020_1/2020/09/04/16-48-06-814_6c7d306a371213c4.webp","destWidth":800,"destHeight":510,"sourceBytes":103932,"destBytes":103932,"author":"<a href=\"https://petapixel.com/author/dlcade/\">DL Cade</a>","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/fstoppers_how_to_photograph_bridal_portraits_on_iphone_phone.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn57@2020_1/2020/09/04/16-48-06-814_6c7d306a371213c4.webp","http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/sample1.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn41@2020_6/2020/09/04/16-48-12-461_1b1e87e5b0ce14ff.webp","http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/sample2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn29@2020_4/2020/09/04/16-48-13-497_bab30093edb7967f.webp","http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/sample3.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn70@2020_1/2020/09/04/16-48-13-221_c569cc5609c4cd75.webp","http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/1-800x326.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn24@2020_4/2020/09/04/16-48-17-109_11aa702663371731.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/PetaPixel?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn14@2020_3/2020/09/04/16-48-04-824_de7088392fb5a9b8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/PetaPixel?i=lSpBYl__4EE:QGO6V5YOKPI:xgp37Vp8p2g":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn3@2020_3/2020/09/04/16-48-17-905_18981c253e4dc860.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/PetaPixel?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn92@2020_1/2020/09/04/16-48-17-572_701e8443590d36d5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/PetaPixel?i=lSpBYl__4EE:QGO6V5YOKPI:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn45@2020_2/2020/09/04/16-48-14-380_c0d80614ad0b6626.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/PetaPixel?i=lSpBYl__4EE:QGO6V5YOKPI:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn6@2020_4/2020/09/04/16-48-18-582_c4821b1497608904.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/PetaPixel?i=lSpBYl__4EE:QGO6V5YOKPI:F7zBnMyn0Lo":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/PetaPixel/~4/lSpBYl__4EE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn13@2020_2/2020/09/04/16-48-12-242_ed6d38b253996134.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599238084514},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","title":"A Primer on Collecting Photo Books","link":"http://petapixel.com/?p=465636","description":"<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks-shelves1-800x464.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"464\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465657\" /></p>\n<p>Revisiting my photography book collection has brought me much enjoyment during the lockdown. A dozen years ago, as the business of photography was good, I used the disposable income to start collecting. In this article, I summarize what I wished I knew back then, not only as a photographer and book collector but also from the perspective of a former art gallery owner and current publisher.</p>\n<h3>Why Collect Photography Books?</h3>\n<p>The prevalent digital consumption of photographs cannot replace the viewing of photography in print. Seeing original prints at exhibits is irreplaceable, but there are only so many museums and galleries even in a major metropolitan area such as the San Francisco Bay Area. Photography books, defined as books where the message is primarily carried by photographs, are the most practical entry into a photographerâ€™s work. </p>\n<p>Unlike magazines, they are physical objects of beauty, with superior production values such as materials, design, and printing. The sequencing, layout, and combination of images and text add layers of meaning and complexity beyond single photographs. Books from a lasting record of works of art. They can rise to the level of works of art themselves, but unlike the art in the museum or gallery, that is a piece of art that you can hold in your hand. </p>\n<p>The simplicity and materiality of the book provide an experience altogether distinct from electronic media. Book pass through ages. In our personal lives, they are often loaded with sentimental value. It can be argued that without books, there would be no modern civilization.</p>\n<p>There are many approaches to photography book collecting that are equally valid. Two ends of the spectrum are to collect solely based on personal taste, ignoring any other external opinions, and to collect based solely on rarity, seeking vintage first editions in excellent condition. I took a middle road, seeing photography books as a vehicle to discover more about photography and deepen my knowledge of its significant artists. </p>\n<p>I was not trying to build an egg nest with the collection, because I wanted foremost to focus on contents and buy books according to interest rather than as an investment opportunity. However, there is no denying that the mercantile aspect of the hobby can be fun and educational, as it mobilizes quite a bit of knowledge: you have to do your research, budget, and prioritize your acquisitions. </p>\n<p>It could be profitable: once I noticed that Mack was going to re-issue Masahisa Fukaseâ€™s <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2FRavens-Masahisa-Fukase%2Fdp%2F1910164836%2F%3Ftag%3D8419-20\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\"><em>Ravens</em></a>, therefore ensuring my continued access to the work, I resold for $1,000 the copy of the Rat Hole Gallery edition bought for less than $100. Note, however, that monetization is always uncertain (the stock market is for that!), and there are indications that the book market is softer than it used to be. Unlike book dealers, even if they seek appreciation in value, collectors generally do not seek to monetize it. Like in all collecting the process can be more satisfying than the resulting ownership.</p>\n<p>Photography books have become highly collectible over the last two decades, thanks to a recent appreciation and recognition of that particular medium, and maybe nostalgia for physical objects. Some books can quickly become worth more than their list price. Once I understood that carefully chosen books can be resold for a profit if needed, I was less hesitant to spend serious money that way. </p>\n<p>There were years when I spent more on books than on photography gear. I sometimes bought multiple copies to resell as a way to finance the hobby, a trade of sorts. While that mercantile aspect of collecting should remain secondary to the love of the books, it is by far the easiest to explain and quantify, kind of like the technical mechanics of photographs, and that is why I will focus on it. The definition of a collectible is: worth more used than what it cost new.</p>\n<h3>The Value Cycle</h3>\n<p>The factors that make any given object collectible are scarcity and demand. Because of the need for quality reproductions, photo books cost much more to print than other books, and therefore they are more expensive. Higher prices result in demand often too small to justify a large print run. Except for some popular coffee-table books, a print run of a few thousand copies is considered large for a photography book. At the same time, although small, the demand often remains steady. Eventually, copies become scarce and valuable. The cycle for desirable books goes like that:</p>\n<p><strong>1.</strong> Book is sold near list price upon release, as novelty is a major selling point.</p>\n<p><strong>2.</strong> Once the novelty wears out, deep discounts (50% is not uncommon on Amazon) become available. In industry jargon, the book has gone from â€œfrontlistâ€� to â€œbacklistâ€�: in catalogs, it is no longer fully described, but merely listed.</p>\n<p><strong>3.</strong> Copies are mostly sold out from the warehouse and large booksellers. At this point, they are available only via independent bookstores, and on Amazon via third-party sellers rather than Amazon itself. Prices start to rise back to list price.</p>\n<p><strong>4.</strong> Book is collectible, with new copies offered for increasing multiples of the original list price, and used copies in excellent condition not too far behind.</p>\n<p>Buying at stage 1 guarantees that you get a copy at list price but at that point, it is possible that the price will go down and the book will not become collectible. A book entering stage 3 is likely to reach stage 4, so for those collectors that focus on the â€œcollectibleâ€� aspect, this may be the safest time to buy. If at that point you are still on the fence, if do not buy and later you find yourself wanting the title, it may no longer be affordable, or even available at all.</p>\n<p>For maximum savings, the best time to buy the books is in stage 2. However, some coveted books never go to this stage and instead quickly sell out upon release and become collectible. This can go pretty fast. Despite its print run of 5,000, the first printing of <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=http%3A%2F%2Ftreasuredlandsbook.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\"><em>Treasured Lands</em></a> (2016) sold out in less than a month. Watching the pre-orders, I initiated a reprint before the book even hit the stores. </p>\n<p>Despite the book not checking most of the usual collectibility factors, in the few months between the fourth printing running out and the fifth printingâ€™s availability, the price of a new copy rose to more than three times the list price, while damaged copies sold over the list price. Pre-publication copies of Alec Sothâ€™s <em>Broken Manual</em> sold at art fairs such as Paris Photo. By the official publication date, not a single copy was available from the publisher. I passed on the limited edition available from the artist because it was priced in the high hundreds of dollars. Copies now start at $6,500.</p>\n<p>Other books never leave stage 2, and their price keeps dropping over time, as there is no demand. My first book, <em>Beautiful North America</em> retails for a fraction of its list price. That book was not my best effort: I only provided images as required by the publisher. Given the target market of discount stores, their effort in editing, design nor printing quality wasnâ€™t the greatest. I regret this book, and in that case, it would seem that the marketâ€™s assessment of its value is correct. However, there also are plenty of absolutely great books that never become collectible and can be bought at bargain prices.</p>\n<h3>Factors to Look For</h3>\n<p><strong>Authorship</strong>. Generally speaking, books that are a compilation of images by several photographers, especially if derived from stock libraries, lack an authorial voice and therefore are seldom considered works of art. That is the case of many coffee-table books. Exceptions include vernacular photography when curated in some clever way (as pioneered by Mandel and Sultanâ€™s Evidence) and some exhibit catalogs.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465658\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465658\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_new_topographics-800x645.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"645\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465658\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465658\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">In 1975, The New Topographics: Photographs of a Man-Altered Landscape was a rare revolutionary exhibit. Even though published 35 years later, the exhibit survey was a much sought after record of it.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Significance/appeal of the artist and work</strong>. Work by artists without institutional art world recognition (exhibited in museums and galleries, reviewed in major publications) is less likely to be collectible and the same principle applies to their books. Some artists have such a reputation and manage so carefully their editions, that almost every one of their books becomes collectible. For a given artist, their earlier work or first breakthrough publication is often more sought after. If their career is, sometimes unfairly, defined by a publication, like Robert Frank by The Americans, it is no surprise that demand for that particular publication will be higher.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465659\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465659\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_americans-800x466.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"466\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465659\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465659\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Although more than 50,000 copies were printed, after Robert Frankâ€™s passing, demand for <em>The Americans</em> quickly drove used copies to more than five times the list price. Reprints have since then reappeared for the work, but not for the monumental catalog of the exhibit dedicated to the book.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Printing quality</strong>. Some older books, such as Brassaiâ€™s <em>Paris de Nuit</em> used to great effect the photogravure printing process to produce rich and sooty blacks. However, generally speaking, photographic printing quality made such great strides in the 1980s that most books published prior look mediocre compared to recent books. The newer books, therefore, provide more enjoyment even though they may not be as valuable as the older, rarer books. </p>\n<p>Some publishers are known for their uncompromising attention to printing quality. In a publisherâ€™s output, not every book is of the same quality. Within their commitment to publishing most of William Egglestonâ€™s work, Steidlâ€™s <em>Chromes</em> volume set was exceptionally well printed, whereas the follow up <em>Los Alamos</em> is just very good. Word has gotten out, and the former is more sought after.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465661\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465661\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_ansel_adams-800x460.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"460\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465661\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465661\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">After finding a copy of the first edition of the Portfolios of Ansel Adams, I was disappointed by the printing quality compared to the modern version. After reviewing several, I found out that the big jump in quality occurred between the 1st edition (1977) and the second edition (1982). Their advertising on the cover page was justified.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Elaborate Productions</strong>. A lot more goes into book production than printing quality, and this can include special materials for casings, unusually large trims, of which the most well-known example is Helmut Newtonâ€™s <em>Sumo</em>, elaborate slipcases, fold-out pages, and unconventional types of binding. For books that exist both as hardcover and softcover, the former is always preferable.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465662\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465662\" style=\"width: 726px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_nazraeli-726x800.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"726\" height=\"800\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465662\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465662\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">A family-owned publisher like Nazraeli pays individual attention to every book, tailoring design, materials (such as the bamboo boards for Michael Kennaâ€™s Hokkaido), slipcases, trims (Jeff Liaoâ€™s Habitat 7 is 24Ã—12 inches, edition of 500) to fit each body of work and create a unique object.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Size of the print run</strong>. Everything being equal, the smaller the print run, the more valuable the book. Coffee-table books destined to the general public often have large print runs above 10,000. As a photography contributor to the two latest National Geographic books about national parks, I received a contract that stated a print run of 50,000 each. </p>\n<p>On the other hand, many publishers specializing in â€œartsyâ€� photography books, especially in Europe, issue print runs in the hundreds. Being geared for the collector market, they often specify the edition size, a piece of information generally not available otherwise. Because of the cost of setting up offset presses and the lack of other economies of scale, the smaller the print run, the higher the production costs per unit, and therefore the higher the retail price. </p>\n<p>In measurable terms such as page per dollar, those books can be an order of magnitude more expensive than mass-produced coffee-table books. Even though those editions are not limited in the sense that the publisher leaves to door open for a reprint, in practice, they rarely occur because demand is limited to collectors.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465663\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465663\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_500ed-800x534.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"534\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465663\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465663\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The copyright page of both those diminutive titles states that they are issued in an edition of 500.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Publisher</strong>. Books from some publishers (for example National Geographic) are hardly ever collectible, while almost everything that some other publishers put out is. This is simply because the laterâ€™s productions always check the four criteria mentioned above so they become known for publishing significant artists, in exquisitely crafted books of generally short print runs. This in turn generates prestige that attracts the best, a self-reinforcing loop. </p>\n<p>Steidl was the gold standard, with their art publishing program partly funded by some other aspects of their publishing enterprises, but while they remain a major force many contemporary photographers seem to have migrated to Mack. </p>\n<p>Non-profit publishing, a model that works well for photography books, is represented by museum or university presses, and associations such as Aperture and Radius. The later puts out books representing a great value given their production quality. The renewed interest in the photography book and the increased accessibility of publishing and printing resources has led to a profusion of very small publishers, whose work often surpasses that of more established ones. Some of the most prized books are artist books, sometimes made by hand.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465665\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465665\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_weston-800x668.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"668\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465665\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465665\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Lodima Press, a small publisher created by a pair of fine art photographers, has used up to 600 line-screen whereas 175 line-screen (which requires 350 PPI) is standard â€“ the Brett Weston portfolios, containing only about a dozen images each, retailed for $60 or more.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Limited editions</strong>. Sometimes, concurrently to a trade, unlimited edition, a limited, numbered edition of the same work is offered. Those books are certainly more valuable, but I normally pass on them because they can expensive, especially if the offering includes a print. I find them worth it when the limited edition is a different and more appealing presentation of the work.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465667\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465667\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_killip-800x484.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"484\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465667\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465667\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Chris Killipâ€™s <em>Here Comes Everybody</em> came in two editions. The trade edition looks like any other photo book. The limited edition (300 copies) is an elaborate production that resembles a photo album with tissue overlays and tipped-in plates, recreating the way the book originated.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>First editions</strong>. <em>Editions</em> refer to a book being re-issued with substantial updates, a different presentation such as softcover vs. a hardcover, or a different publisher. They are more relevant to guidebooks or technology tutorials, but even art books are sometimes re-issued with additional images or commentary. Editions are often mentioned as part of the title. </p>\n<p><em>Printings</em> refer to the book being re-issued in identical or near-identical form. They are indicated on the copyright page. If you donâ€™t find a mention such as â€œ2nd printingâ€�, there may be a series of numbers on the copyright page such as â€œ10 9 8 7 6 5 6 5 4 3 2â€�, with the last number representing the printing. Sometimes, only the year of the printing is indicated, and you need to research the printing history of the book to figure out which printing it is. </p>\n<p>Even if a book has a large total print run, the number of copies of the first edition and first printing (sometimes abbreviated as first edition) can be much smaller, which makes it valuable to collectors seeking rare books.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465668\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465668\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_decisive_moment-800x454.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"454\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465668\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465668\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">When Steidl reissued Henri Cartier-Bressonâ€™s <em>The Decisive Moment</em>, I bought a copy to use for reading, as my 1952 first edition copy was literally falling apart. Despite the availability of the reprint, the value of such a tattered copy didnâ€™t fall, while copies in excellent condition continued to command high prices.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Condition</strong>. Everything else being equal, in the collector world, a bookâ€™s condition is the most important factor in determining its value because even if an old book is not particularly rare, a copy in excellent condition is. From worst to best, the following terms are used: poor, fair/acceptable, good, very good, near fine, fine/like new, new. </p>\n<p>Most collectors consider that â€œgood isnâ€™t good enoughâ€�, and seek books in condition at least â€œvery goodâ€�: minor signs of wear, but no tears and no markings. It is important to take good care of oneâ€™s books. The better the book is, the more likely one is to share it with others, so the more likely it will get worn out no matter how careful you are. For this reason, some collectors like to buy two copies of titles they are excited about, one to read, and the other to keep in pristine condition, under the publisherâ€™s shrinkwrap.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_muir1-800x334.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"334\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465669\" /></p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465670\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465670\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_muir2-800x255.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"255\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465670\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465670\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Three printings of the same book (John Muirâ€™s Our National Park) in fair, good and fine condition.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Removable elements</strong>. Some books were issued with a dust jacket. When buying used, a bit of research is necessary to figure out if that was the case, since dust jackets are often missing from used offerings. A first edition (later printing) copy of John Muirâ€™s <em>Our National Parks</em> with a dust jacket is worth ten times more than one without. Because of the bookâ€™s size, the dust jacket for Edward Westonâ€™s <em>My Camera at Pt. Lobos</em> is frequently damaged, so a dust jacket in excellent condition is particularly rare. To separate photographs from captions or commentary a separate booklet may be included, for instance when the book is printed full bleed like Sebastio Salgadoâ€™s major projects.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465671\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465671\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_belly_band-800x586.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"586\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465671\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465671\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Quite a few Japanese books include belly bands. Easily lost or damaged, not mentioned by the publisher, they sometimes contribute to most a bookâ€™s value.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Signed copies</strong>. There is a saying that the difference between a poster and an art print is the artistâ€™s signature. It is not entirely true, because the printing process matters a great deal. Still, an artistâ€™s signature helps in conferring to a book the status of an art object. Some signatures are rarer than others, and this varies from book to book. </p>\n<p>The very social Ansel Adams signed many more books than Edward Weston. When <em>My Camera at Pt. Lobos</em> was published, Edward Weston was sick with Parkinsonâ€™s disease, so signed copies are extremely rare. The proper spot for a signature is normally the half-title page â€“ the page where the only type is the title. Signatures can be obtained at lectures, gallery openings, and of course book signings. Pre-signed copies are sometimes available from the publisher or a gallery. Inscribed copies include, in addition to the signature, an inscription to a person. When the person is not of particular note, the inscription devaluates the signature, however, when they are, the inscription makes the book a valuable â€œassociation copyâ€�.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465672\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465672\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks_inscribed-800x507.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"507\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465672\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465672\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">I like my books personalized as a memento of a connection with the artist. A book just signed may have a higher resale value, but I plan to hold onto those.</figcaption></figure>\n<h3>What to Collect?</h3>\n<p>If you buy books that you like, whether they appreciate doesnâ€™t matter. With experience, you will be able to spot good books, well-made, and with inspired works in any genre, collectible or not. However, if you stick only to your present interests, you may be missing a lot of the vast world of photography. There are so many photography books out there that knowing where to start can be daunting. Anybody who studies literature reads through a list of classics. Photography has also its classics, representing a consensus of curators and critics.</p>\n<p>In the 20th century, the history of the photography book was kind of hidden within the history of photography. Since the beginning of this century, its narrative as a full medium has emerged. In 2001, Andrew Roth published the first authoritative English-language study of photography books, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2FBook-101-Books-Photographic-Twentieth%2Fdp%2F0967077443%2F%3Ftag%3D8419-20\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">The Book of 101 Books: Seminal Photographic Books of the Twentieth Century</a>. </p>\n<p>Three years later, Martin Parr and Gerry Badger vastly expanded Rothâ€™s survey with <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2FPhotobook-History-Gerry-Badger-2004-11-19%2Fdp%2FB01K0TUUR8%2F%3Ftag%3D8419-20\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">The Photobook: A History (Volume I)</a>, followed by <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2FPhotobook-History-Gerry-Badger-2004-11-19%2Fdp%2FB01K0TUUR8%2F%3Ftag%3D8419-20\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Volume 2</a> (2006) and <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2FPhotobook-History-III-Martin-Parr%2Fdp%2F0714866776%2F%3Ftag%3D8419-20\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Volume 3</a> (2014). Those foundational works form an excellent introduction to photography books and feature a wealth of titles in an engaging format. </p>\n<p>Note, however, that their selected books share the authorial stance of an extended essay and a specific social/cultural theme, leaving out for example most of the American modernists, and omitting many genres. Three that interest me are landscape, including nature landscape (surveys: <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2F%2Fblog%2Fansel-adams-photography-books%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Ansel Adams</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2F%2Fblog%2Feliot-porter-books%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Eliot Porter</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2F%2Fblog%2Fphilip-hyde-books%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Philip Hyde</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2F%2Fblog%2Fgalen-rowell-books%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Galen Rowell</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2Fblog%2F15-more-classic-color-nature-photography-books%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">15 more classic color nature photography books</a>), nude, and all photographer retrospective monographs. All those books about books except Parr/Badger Volume 3, have become collectible themselves. Unfortunately, they have also caused many of the books featured to rise in price and become quite expensive. It wouldnâ€™t be the worse idea to buy Volume 3 now and see which of the books mentioned are still reasonably priced. The success of the Parr/Badger series has spawned several books surveying a particular region or countryâ€™s photography books.</p>\n<p>For reviews of new titles, blogs are your best bet. Some of my favorites include <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=http%3A%2F%2F5b4.blogspot.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">5B4</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fphotobookjournal.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">PhotoBook Journal</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fcollectordaily.com%2Fcategory%2Fphotobooks%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Collector Daily</a>, and <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.photoeye.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Photo Eye</a>. To see what titles caught the attention of the blogosphere in a given year, refer to an initiative called the â€œphotobook meta-listâ€� that attempts to aggregate many â€œbest of the yearâ€� lists. </p>\n<p>The first photobook meta-list was created by Marc Feustel in <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.marcfeustel.com%2Feyecurious%2Fphotobooks-2011-and-the-winner-is%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2011</a>. I subsequently maintained the meta-list (<a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2Fblog%2F2013%2F02%2F01%2Fbest-photobooks-2012-the-meta-list%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2012</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2Fblog%2F2013%2F12%2F09%2Fbest-photobooks-2013-the-meta-list%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2013</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2Fblog%2Fbest-photobooks-2014-the-meta-list%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2014</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2Fblog%2Fbest-photobooks-2015-the-meta-list%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2015</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2Fblog%2Fbest-photobooks-2016-the-meta-list%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2016</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.terragalleria.com%2Fblog%2Fbest-photobooks-2017-the-meta-list%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2017</a>). Since 2015, Viory Schellekens has been compiling another meta-list, and discovering that hers was more meticulous and informative than mine, I decided to pass the baton. Here are the links to Vioryâ€™s lists: <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.facebook.com%2Fviorys%2Fposts%2F10207042980207205\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2015</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.facebook.com%2FViory.Schellekens%2Fposts%2F1141053922630276\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2016</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=http%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2Fmetalist2017\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2017</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fbit.ly%2F2FdaUPW\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2018</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.facebook.com%2FViory.Schellekens%2Fposts%2F2509730949095893\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">2019</a>. In the winter of 2016, Source Magazine used the methodology of the meta-list to create <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.source.ie%2Fphotobook%2Fgreatest.php\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">a list of the greatest photobooks of all time</a>.</p>\n<h3>Where to Find Books</h3>\n<p>Amazon offers discounts on new titles and free shipping, but their packaging is often inadequate, frequently resulting in bumped corners and other damage. They sell photobooks as commodities, unlike the bookstores specializing in photography books such as <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.photoeye.com%2Fbookstore%2Findex.cfm%3Fcatalog%3DZJ289\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Photo-Eye</a> in Santa Fe or <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.dashwoodbooks.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Dashwood Books</a> in NYC. Those stores are run by people who know and love the medium, and are often able to procure hard to find books, foreign titles, or signed copies. </p>\n<p>If a title sells fast via other channels, the publisher may not send copies to Amazon at all, since of all bookstores, Amazon terms are the most unfavorable to publishers. As a result, if you placed a pre-order or order on Amazon for that â€œhotâ€� title, by the time you realize that it will not be fulfilled, the title may already have entered collectible territory.</p>\n<p>If you are knowledgeable, you can sometimes find bargains browsing used bookstores, and also make trades. However, the better the selection, the better the owner will be aware of the value of their books. In the San Francisco Bay Area, Moeâ€™s Books in Berkeley has the best selection. Such places are particularly valuable because you get to see in person many books. Their number has been declining, as the market has been moving away from brick-and-mortar towards online.</p>\n<p>Although not specializing in photography books, used bookstore networks such as <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.abebooks.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Abebooks</a>, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.alibris.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Alibris</a>, and <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.biblio.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Biblio</a> give access to reliable professional used booksellers, especially those affiliated with the Antiquarian Booksellersâ€™ Association of America, whose meticulous descriptions can be relied upon. The best way to mobilize those vast resources is to use the bookstore meta search engine <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bookfinder.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Bookfinder.com</a>. </p>\n<p>I try to buy books directly from artists when possible in order to obtain a signature. It also helps them financially, since a book sold through retail earns the author only 5-10% of the list price. If you really get bitten by the photography book bug, you may want to travel attend some of the fairs and festivals dedicated to the medium that takes place annually. </p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/photobooks-shelves2-800x471.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"471\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465673\" /></p>\n<p>Collecting photography books is a great hobby that I highly recommend provided that you donâ€™t plan to move too often.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><em><strong>About the author</strong>: QT Luong was the first to photograph all America&#8217;s 62 National Parks &#8212; in large format. 00:48:04","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","title":"Before and After: A Photo Series About COVID-19 Isolation in Toronto","link":"http://petapixel.com/?p=465857","description":"<p><center><div class=\"fluid-iframe\" style=\"max-width: 800px;\"><div class=\"fluid-iframe__inner\" style=\"padding-top:56.25%\"><iframe allowfullscreen></iframe></div></div></center></p>\n<p>&#8220;Before and After&#8221; is a photo series by photographer <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bradfreemanfilms.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Brad Freeman</a> that documents the isolation he has experienced in Toronto, Canada, during the COVID-19 pandemic. His brother <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Flosslesscreative.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Ryan</a> also made the above 4.5-minute short documentary about Brad&#8217;s experience in creating the work.</p>\n<p>When Toronto launched phase 1 of its reopening after its major lockdown, Brad went out with his Leica M3 and created 40 photos on black-and-white 35mm film.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/005045030027-800x531.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"531\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465860\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/005045060020-800x531.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"531\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465861\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/005045070032-800x531.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"531\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465862\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/005045110005-800x531.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"531\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465863\" /></p>\n<p>&#8220;Being isolated during the height of the pandemic felt like a dream, it was both familiar and strange at the same time,&#8221; Brad says. &#8220;I set out to find some sort of normalcy only to realize the world as we knew it had changed. The streets were completely abandoned, a surreal version of our new reality.&#8221;</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/005045110030-800x531.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"531\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465864\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/005045110036-800x531.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"531\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465865\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/005045120019-800x531.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"531\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465866\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/005045130005-800x531.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"531\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465867\" /></p>\n<p>&#8220;I had a lot of anxiety during lockdown, it was a time full of uncertainty,&#8221; Brad says. &#8220;Being a creative person I was looking for some sort of outlet after being alone for 3 months. I went outside when phase 1 of reopening the city began, but everything seemed to be abandoned. </p>\n<p>&#8220;It only made me feel more uncomfortable. This uncanny feeling of strangeness and emptiness comes through in the photos.&#8221;</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/005045140011-800x531.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" 00:48:04","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","title":"This Guy Turned His Game Boy Camera Into a Functional Webcam","link":"http://petapixel.com/?p=465964","description":"<p><div class=\"fluid-iframe\" style=\"max-width: 800px;\"><div class=\"fluid-iframe__inner\" style=\"padding-top:56.25%\"><iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/sF_jSpED8xE\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></div></div></p>\n<p>A couple of days ago a user on r/Gameboy asked the community if there was any way to turn his Game Boy Camera into a functioning webcam so that (in his words) &#8220;I can be an a** to people I don&#8217;t respect.&#8221; Well, someone came through and showed that it is actually possible to do this.</p>\n<p>The whole thing started with user u/eye_for_an_homonculi on the r/Gameboy subreddit, who had a bit of a passive aggressive axe to grind. Earlier this week, he asked the subreddit if there was any way to use his Game Boy Camera as a webcam in order to &#8220;piss off&#8221; some people who had placed some ridiculous streaming rules onto a &#8220;professional development test&#8221; he had to take. </p>\n<p>Irony aside, after putting the question out there, retro gamer and hardware modder <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.instagram.com%2Fbernard.c%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Bernard Capulong</a> came through. It <em>is</em> possible&#8230; although it&#8217;s not exactly simple.</p>\n<p>You can see his setup here:</p>\n<p><center></p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">it was my destiny to answer this question in the nerdiest way imaginable <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Ft.co%2FnYDaz63B3K\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">pic.twitter.com/nYDaz63B3K</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Bernard (@bernardcapulong) <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Ftwitter.com%2Fbernardcapulong%2Fstatus%2F1300912062269325312%3Fref_src%3Dtwsrc%255Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">September 1, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p> <script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></center></p>\n<p>According to Capulong, Step 1 of this process is &#8220;don&#8217;t.&#8221; </p>\n<p>If you choose to ignore Step 1, the rest of the setup includes combining all of the following:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>A Game Boy Camera cartridge</li>\n<li>A Super Game Boy 2 cartridge</li>\n<li>An Analogue Super Nt or a Super Nintendo/Super Famicom with an upscaler like a Retrotink</li>\n<li>A Capture Card</li>\n<li>An External Microphone</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Put all of these together, and you&#8217;ve turned your Game Boy Camera into a webcam that can be used with Streamlabs OBS or Zoom no problem. In fact, the video up top is a converted recording from a Zoom meeting.</p>\n<p>Granted, in terms of image quality and effort-to-reward ratio, this is probably a step in the <em>wrong</em> direction&#8230; but you have to give the man points for ingenuity and style. And if you happen to run in some nerdy circles, this would earn you some serious street cred.</p>\n<p>Watch the video sample up top to see how this mod turned out, and <a href=\"https://petapixel.com/?s=%22game+boy+camera%22\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\">click here</a> if you want to see lots more Game Boy Camera hackery. </p>\n<p>(via <a 00:48:04","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","title":"Canon to Release Sub-$999 Full-Frame EOS R Camera in 2021: Report","link":"http://petapixel.com/?p=465799","description":"<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/canonfeat-800x420.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"420\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465808\" /></p>\n<p>Over the past couple of years, the barrier to entry for full-frame has dropped significantlyâ€”starting with the <a href=\"https://petapixel.com/2019/02/13/canon-unveils-the-eos-rp-the-smallest-and-lightest-full-frame-eos/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\">$1,300 Canon EOS RP</a>, and followed by the almost-as-cheap <a href=\"https://petapixel.com/2020/07/21/nikon-unveils-the-z5-its-entry-level-full-frame-mirrorless-camera/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\">$1,400 Nikon Z5</a>. But it seems Canon may be planning to release an <em>even cheaper</em> EOS R camera in 2021.</p>\n<p>This report comes from our friends at <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.canonrumors.com%2Fa-budget-eos-r-body-is-coming-in-the-first-half-of-2021-cr2%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\"><em>Canon Rumors</em></a>, who were told that &#8220;a new entry-level full-frame EOS R camera&#8221; would be announced in 2021 with a price tag that comes in under $999. </p>\n<p>No specs were shared, and this is still a ways out so expect this camera to be a bit of a &#8220;moving target&#8221; at Canon as of this writing, but the fact that this is even being considered is wild. Few cameras (if any) manage to hold their MSRP/starting price for longer than a few months, so if Canon is willing to release this camera at $999 (or less), they expect to sell most of them at $100 or $200 below that price, bringing the full-frame barrier to entry all the way down into the $700 range for a brand new camera.</p>\n<p>Case in point: the Canon EOS RP, which debuted at $1,300 less than two years ago, <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.adorama.com%2Fcarp.html%3Fkbid%3D67085\" rel=\"norewrite follow external noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">can be had for $1,000 brand new</a> as of this writing.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465805\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465805\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/carp_1-800x500.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"500\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465805\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465805\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The Canon EOS RP debuted at $1,300 in February of 2019. You can get one for just $1,000 today.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>As <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.canonwatch.com%2Fcan-canon-make-an-r-series-camera-less-expensive-than-the-eos-rp-yes-a-canon-exec-said%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\"><em>Canon Watch</em> points out</a>, this isn&#8217;t pure speculation&#8230; a Canon Europe Technical Support Manager admitted that they could make an even cheaper full-frame mirrorless camera than the EOS RP way back in April of 2019. </p>\n<p>But being <em>able</em> to make this camera and actually planning to make it are two very different things, and the &#8220;race to the bottom&#8221; consequences of releasing a brand new, sub-$999 full-frame camera could be significant. We all love cheaper gear&#8230; but Canon would likely lose money selling this camera in an attempt to get people hooked on the RF mount and its (mostly expensive) lenses.</p>\n<p>Still, with each new mirrorless camera release we see more comments asking for a stills-only full-frame camera that doesn&#8217;t bother with the expense or technology required to integrate high-quality video. Maybe that&#8217;s what Canon has in store for this ultra-affordable entry-level camera. Or maybe they&#8217;ll cut some other corner like leaving out the EVF. 00:48:04","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","title":"First Look: Is the Fuji XF 50mm f/1.0 the Ultimate X-Mount Portrait Lens?","link":"http://petapixel.com/?p=465897","description":"<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/ultimateportraitfeat-800x420.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"420\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465901\" /></p>\n<p>A while back, Fujifilm announced that they were working on a 33mm f/1 lens. Recently it was announced that they had scrapped that lens to work on a 50mm f/1, which would result in a more compact lens. With a super-fast 56mm f/1.2 already in the Fuji lens lineup, will a 50mm f/1 be different enough? We were lucky enough to get a sample 50mm f/1 to test out for a short while.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://petapixel.com/2020/09/03/fujifilm-unveils-xf-50mm-f-1-0-lens-the-fastest-fuji-lens-ever-made/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\">The XF50mm f/1</a> is a chunky lens, which is to be expected given itâ€™s fast aperture. Despite its size, the lens has a minimalistic design with no switches and only an aperture ring. The aperture ring is a bit easier to change than some of Fujiâ€™s other lenses, which some photographers may like, but I found myself accidentally bumping it and changing apertures on more than one occasion. </p>\n<p>If you plan on manually focusing a lot, the focusing ring is nice and large and has a smooth throw with 120Âº of rotation to make manual focusing easy and precise. Like all other weather-resistant XF Lenses, it is protected against moisture and dust, and shouldnâ€™t have any issues when shooting in less than ideal environments. </p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PT_07_XF50mmF1_0_T4_Diagonal-1-800x648.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"648\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465902\" /></p>\n<p>The lens has a 77mm front filter thread, which is larger than most of Fujiâ€™s lenses, but a common size for CPL and ND/VND filters. It has 12 elements in 9 groups, with 1 aspherical element and 2 ED elements. </p>\n<p>It comes in at a hefty 845 grams, only about 100 grams less than the XF50-140mm f/2.8. The lens alone is just over 4 inches long, add the lens hood and youâ€™re looking at almost 6.5 inches. Even though it feels good to hold, itâ€™s not likely to be a lens youâ€™re always reaching for due to its size. </p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PT_05_XF50mmF1_0_T4Top-1-800x680.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"680\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465903\" /></p>\n<h3>Image Quality and Performance</h3>\n<p>Fuji went all-in on making this lens a great performer wide open, and the image quality supports it. The XF50mm f/1 is sharper than the XF56mm f/1.2 wide open, and it becomes more apparent the closer you get to your subject. </p>\n<p>As you stop down the lenses, the sharpness becomes more equal, but if youâ€™re buying an f/1 lens, chances are you want to shoot wide open. The close focus distance is very similar between the two lenses, right around 70cm, which is more than close enough for tight headshots. </p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/15ft_Side_By_Side-800x534.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"534\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465904\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/4ft_Side_By_Side-800x534.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"534\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465905\" /></p>\n<p>Light flaring and chromatic aberrations are minimal. The only time I saw any blue fringing was when shooting directly up until the sun through some leaves, and even then, itâ€™s a lot less than some f/1.4 and f/1.8 lenses Iâ€™ve used in similar situations. </p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/DSCF4743-800x534.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"534\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465906\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/DSCF4743-Edit-800x533.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465907\" /></p>\n<p>Autofocus speeds on the 50mm are average compared to the rest of the Fuji lineup. While the focus is precise and accurate, the speed isnâ€™t as fast as some of Fujiâ€™s fast primes and zooms, which is to be expected given the amount and size of the glass inside the lens. Face and Eye-AF worked well when tested on an X-T3 and X-T4. For videographers, the focus transitions are smooth, but itâ€™s not the quietest lens from Fuji. Focus motor noise is noticeable when using the in-camera mic, but it wasnâ€™t present when using a shotgun mic on the hotshoe. </p>\n<h3>Sample Images</h3>\n<p>These sample photos were taken with the rel=\"norewrite follow external noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">X-T3</a> and <a For?</h3>\n<p>Coming in at $500 more than the <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.adorama.com%2Fifj56xf.html%3Fkbid%3D67085\" rel=\"norewrite follow external noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">56mm f/1.2</a>, the $1,499 price tag on the 50mm f/1 can be a tough pill to swallow for some, especially considering itâ€™s only a half-stop faster. But for those looking for superior image quality from a lens, especially when shooting wide open, the 50mm f/1 is hard to beat. </p>\n<p>While the focal range could be useful in everyday shooting and street photography, the size is likely to be a turn off to many for consistent use. For those who center their work around portraits, weddings, commercial and studio work, this lens is definitely worth taking a look at. </p>\n<hr />\n<p>The Fujifilm XF50mm f/1 R WR is expected to ship September 25th, and can be pre-ordered <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.thepixelconnection.com%2Ffujiflm-xf50mm-f1-0-r-wr-black.html\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">here</a>.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><em><strong>About the author</strong>: Ihor Balaban is a photographer and store manager of the camera store Pixel Connection in Avon, Ohio.
