00:48:04","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","title":"Teardown Reveals â€˜Overheating Timerâ€™ Chip Inside the Canon EOS R6","link":"http://petapixel.com/?p=466027","description":"<p><a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fkolarivision.com%2Farticles%2Ffull_spectrum_conversion%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\"></a><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/timer_feat-800x420.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"420\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466036\" /></p>\n<p>Here at <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fkolarivision.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Kolari Vision</a>, we love tearing into the newest camera gears to learn how they work and if they can be modded for <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fkolarivision.com%2Fwhat-is-infrared-photography%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">infrared photography</a>, full spectrum photography, or other things. Weâ€™ve been really excited about the R5/R6 release, and had plans to add some cooling mods and overhaul it into a proper video camera. </p>\n<p>Reports from <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.eoshd.com%2Fnews%2Fcanon-eos-r5-so-called-overheat-timer-defeated-by-a-single-screw-in-battery-door%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\"><em>EOSHD</em></a> that Canon uses an overheat timer rather than actual temperature readings left us a bit disappointed, and calls into question whether physically cooling down the camera can actually give any more shooting time. </p>\n<p>Andrew Reid was able to bypass this timer by using a screw to override the safety shutoff switch in the battery door compartment and do a hard shutdown during recording, but this seems to corrupt video files. â€œMath Classâ€� on Baidu recently showed that removing the clock battery can also bypass this timer. A firmware update by Canon on the R5 has also recently extended the shooting length by a seemingly arbitrary time, showing that software can absolutely affects shutdown times. </p>\n<p>These data so far suggest that the camera keeps internal time, keeps time when the camera is off, and uses these values to influence if shooting can resume. A hard shutdown corrupts some data being written, preventing a time limit from being established. The clock battery removal suggests that without a clock keeping time while the camera is off, there is no way to establish a countdown timer, and the camera defaults to zero on the shooting time. </p>\n<p>With this knowledge, we wanted to investigate how the camera functions without a clock battery, could we identify a physical clock chip on the board, and is there a more advanced modification that could be made to interrupt the clock timer communication without affecting date/time settings. Right now we only have the R6 to work with, but we suspect the R5 works similarly. If anyone has an R5, please contact us.</p>\n<p>So first, letâ€™s start with the clock battery. It can be found on the back of the main circuit board.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/battery-1-800x420.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"420\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466044\" /></p>\n<p>The first thing we wanted to check was, how does missing the battery affect general performance? The clock is of course reset, but on other Canon cameras it has prevented saving shooting settings and custom settings, which would be deal breaker. </p>\n<p>So we set some custom menus, changed some shooting values, and some menu settings, and then proceeded to remove the clock battery. Leaving the board completely powered off without any battery source for about 30 minutes, we re-assembled the camera sans battery and checked it out. We received the expected prompt for time/date, but were pleasantly surprised to find the rest of our settings were still there. Nice! </p>\n<p>We also found that the camera keeps time as long as the main battery is in place, even when turned off. </p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/timerchip2-800x534.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"534\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466033\" /></p>\n<p>Next up, could we trace out where the battery leads connect to. Visually checking, the leads from the battery immediately go down into the board to a middle layer, so we could not visually trace them out. Oh well, we have a multimeter! </p>\n<p>Running a continuity check from the leads, I was able to trace the right lead to the common ground right away. The left positive lead was a bit harder, but the trace must come out somewhere, so I went around testing components throughout the board on both sides. A bit tedious, but I was able to identify only one chip that the battery feeds into.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/timerchip-800x534.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"534\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466031\" /></p>\n<p>We needed a microscope to read the chip, but were able to identify it as the RX8130 Real Time Clock, complete with a 59 page documentation PDF. Bingo. This is what keeps time.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/chip.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"219\" height=\"200\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-466034\" /></p>\n<p>The wiring diagram for the RX8130 looks like this (see below). I was able to identify the clock battery feeds into pin 10 through a 470 ohm resister. Pin 7 also connects to ground. Interestingly, pin 6, 2, and 3 either connect to nothing, or connect to something directly going down under the board. We need to remove the chip to see more definitively, but potentially they are not used.</p>\n<p>Pin 4 from the documentation is used for the frequency out, and this connects to a 6 pin chip immediately to the right that reads only pQ on it, hopefully someone has more insight on this chip. Pin 5 leads elsewhere on the board we canâ€™t identify. Pins 1 connects to a distant BGA mounted chip with what looks like a smoothing capacitor connection to ground. Pins 8 and 9 also connect elsewhere we canâ€™t trace yet and also feature smoothing capacitors.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/manual-800x537.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"537\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466035\" /></p>\n<p>So far, thatâ€™s all the progress we made. We like to be transparent in what our mods do, so we decided to open up our research here as we go. </p>\n<p>Based on this chipâ€™s documentation, our basic understanding is that this chip receives power from the main board first, and if there is no power there, it draws power from the backup button cell battery. The chip is able to keep time, and can output time data, as well as other stored data, there is some room for general bit storage. The chip is also able to send interrupt and data signals back out, but so far it doesnâ€™t look like those pins are necessarily being used. Canon may not be using the internal interrupt and timer functions, and may be doing that elsewhere using this chip as only a timekeeper.</p>\n<p>Our next plan is to verify this with an R5, and pop the chip out and see if we can measure any signals on a scope during the actual overheat event. In the meantime, from how the settings storage is handled, it looks like we should be able to just remove the clock battery, or put the clock battery on a separate toggle switch. Also, we can of course bypass the hard reset screw approach Andrew Reid did, and just put a hard switch on the power leads to the main board. We can even control these switch with a microcontroller and force a hard reset through software if needed, say something like, after you hit record the camera cycles a hard shutdown after 15 minutes, or cycles an ordered shutdown paired with a clock reset as a coordinated event. </p>\n<p>We also want to check how the camera behaves if there is no clock power even when the camera is on. I suspect a hard error, but who knows! BUT WE NEED AN R5 to start. Please, internet. If you have one you can loan or sell us, weâ€™ll share what we find publicly and give you first access to our Frankenstein bypassed ultimate R5 mod.</p>\n<p><strong>One final important comment</strong>: While it seems definitive that Canon is using a timer circuit to shut down the R5 in overheating, we can only speculate as to why for now. It is possible that it&#8217;s there to &#8220;cripple&#8221; the camera, but itâ€™s still very possible that there are some overheating concerns for this weather sealed body, and they are shutting down based on a timer schedule for now for longevity.</p>\n<p>I would approach any of these bypass strategies with extreme caution, as they will probably not only void your warranty, but potentially fry your camera from extended shooting. We still plan to open up the R5 and add a heatsink thatâ€™s thermally fused to the overheating chips and card slots, and attach this heatsink to an aluminum cage for dissipation, as well an active fan. In this cooled context, we expect to keep the R5 very cool for extended shooting, but it would require the timer shutdown to be bypassed.</p>\n<p>So let us know what you think and if you have any chip insight! What would you like us to try next?</p>\n<hr />\n<p><em><strong>About the author</strong>: Ilija Melentijevic is a scientist/photographer and owner of <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fkolarivision.com\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Kolari Vision</a>, an infrared camera conversion business based in New Jersey. class=\"fluid-iframe\" style=\"max-width: 800px;\"><div class=\"fluid-iframe__inner\" style=\"padding-top:56.25%\"><iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/TTnwYmEWvPI\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></div></div></p>\n<p>Photographers can learn a lot about composition and color theory from great cinematography. Case in point: in this video, filmmaker Sareesh Sudhakaran of <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fchannel%2FUC7gBcKzHKc0oOR5-XiWdlFQ\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Wolfcrow</a> explains how great movies will often use the &#8216;Three Color Rule&#8217; to capture and keep a viewer&#8217;s attention.</p>\n<p>We&#8217;ve shared many tips, tutorials, and breakdowns about <a href=\"https://petapixel.com/?s=color+theory\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\">color theory</a> over the years, but Sudhakaran&#8217;s video takes a simple approach. He picks a few critically acclaimed films like <em>Joker</em>, <em>Her</em>, <em>Amelie</em>, and <em>Drive</em>, and shows you how the cinematographer, DOP, and editors used the so-called &#8220;Three Color Rule&#8221; to focus the audience&#8217;s attention on the story.</p>\n<p>The basic rule is as follows:</p>\n<blockquote><p>You have three important colors in your frame: about 60% of the frame is the predominant or primary color, about 30% is a secondary color, and the last 10% is an accent color.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In the movie <em>Her</em>, for example, Sudhakaran identifies the primary color as a brown, the secondary color as red, and the accent color as a barely noticeable blueish shade:</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/her_colors-800x440.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"440\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465983\" /></p>\n<p>Of course, it&#8217;s not always this obvious, but great films are remarkably consistent about the color grading choices they make in order to maintain a mood, direct the audience&#8217;s attention, and sometimes outright tell the view what&#8217;s going on, using color as the vehicle for that message.</p>\n<p>This video is a great reminder of the powerful role that color can play in bringing a series of workâ€”or even a single, still imageâ€”together into a cohesive whole. Everybody&#8217;s approach to using color will (and should) differ, but if you&#8217;re trying to develop a personal &#8220;style&#8221; that is recognizable, it would be foolish to pay close attention to things like genre, composition, lighting, posing, props, or even camera brand, and leave color as an afterthought.</p>\n<p>As <a href=\"https://petapixel.com/2020/06/26/an-ode-to-harry-gruyaert-a-master-of-color-photography/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\">the great Harry Gruyaert</a> once said, &#8220;if you shoot in color, it has to be the first thing.&#8221;</p>\n<p>(via <a Fujifilm has unveiled the <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.adorama.com%2Fifj50xf.html\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Fujinon XF 50mm f/1.0 WR</a>â€”the fastest lens Fuji has ever made and the world&#8217;s first f/1.0 autofocus lens for mirrorless cameras.</p>\n<p>Fuji has dubbed this lens &#8220;The One&#8221;, and is promising that it will change the way you work by providing the incredibly shallow depth-of-field and extreme low-light performance of an f/1.0 lens <em>without</em> sacrificing autofocus or skimping on the weather sealing.</p>\n<p>â€œWeâ€™re really excited about the XF50mmF1.0 R WR,â€� says Fujifilm&#8217;s Victor Ha, senior director of marketing and product management at Fujifilm North America. â€œNot only is it the fastest interchangeable lens Fujifilm has ever produced, but itâ€™s also an incredible tool for visual storytellers to use in telling their stories because its autofocus can achieve critical focus at very shallow depth of fields.â€�</p>\n<p>You can get an overview of the new lens in the video below:</p>\n<p><div class=\"fluid-iframe\" style=\"max-width: 800px;\"><div class=\"fluid-iframe__inner\" style=\"padding-top:56.25%\"><iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/soUkgIR6g-c\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></div></div></p>\n<p>Optically, the lens is made up of 12 elements in 9 groupsâ€”including one aspherical element and two extra-low dispersion (ED) elementâ€”which pair with a 9-blade rounded aperture that goes from f/1.0 to f/16. As you might imagine, this lens is all about that maximum aperture and what it will allow you to do&#8230; not just obliterate the background, but in low-light as well.</p>\n<p>At f/1.0, the lens allows the Fuji X-Pro3 and X-T4 cameras&#8217; autofocus systems to operate at just -7EV (previous limit was -6EV), promising &#8220;fast and precise low-light autofocus, even in near-darkness.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Speaking of autofocus, the lens&#8217; AF system is powered by a direct current (DC) motor that relies on the Fuji X-Series PDAF for directions. However, if you want to go full manual, you&#8217;ll find a nice looooong 120Â° focus throw on the focus ring itself, making it possible to actually nail focus with a little help from from peaking and focus assist.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/fujilens_2.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"541\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-465782\" /></p>\n<p>OF course, in order to pack all of this into a single lens, Fuji wasn&#8217;t exactly able to make this a &#8220;compact&#8221; optic. The 50mm f/1.0 features a 77mm filter thread, measures 4.07-inches (103.5mm) long and weighs in at 1.86lb (845g), which is&#8230; hefty for a 50mm. </p>\n<p>However, that does include an autofocus motor <em>and full weather sealing</em>, making this a &#8220;WR&#8221; lens that&#8217;s protected against dust and moisture, and can be used reliably at temperatures as low as 14Â°F (-10Â°C).</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s a closer look at this impressive optic:</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PT_02_XF50mmF1_0_lensSide-800x500.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" 00:48:04","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","title":"Can Pixel Shift Compete with a Bigger, Higher Resolution Sensor?","link":"http://petapixel.com/?p=466002","description":"<p><div class=\"fluid-iframe\" style=\"max-width: 800px;\"><div class=\"fluid-iframe__inner\" style=\"padding-top:56.25%\"><iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/s27PieFs5CE\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></div></div></p>\n<p>In a pseudo Part III to their sensor size comparison series, Jay P Morgan and Kenneth Merrill over at <em>The Slanted Lens</em> decided to answer a question that popped up several times in the comments of a previous video: can the pixel shifting on a Micro Four Thirds or full-frame camera match the output of a 100MP medium format sensor? </p>\n<p>The three cameras being tested here are the Olympus OM-D E-M1 Mark III, the Sony a7R IV, and the Fujifilm GFX 100, and the point was simple: limitations of pixel shift photography aside, can the output from the Olympus and Sony&#8217;s respective &#8216;pixel shift&#8217; modes out-perform the standard, single-shot performance of the 100MP medium format GFX 100?</p>\n<p>The side-by-side test involved capturing photos of The Broad art museum, since its architectural style and location was ideally suited for highlighting issues like aliasing and any problems with dynamic range.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/Pixel-Shift-Thumbnail-2_DSCF0012_crop_sm-800x450.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466005\" /></p>\n<p>First, they compared the full-frame Sony to the medium format GFX. When using the pixel shift mode with the Sony, you have two options: a 4-image stack that spits out a sharper version at the same 61MP resolution as a single shot; or a 16-image stack that produces a whopping 240MP file.</p>\n<p>You can see side-by-side comparisons of the output from the Fuji and the Sony (in both modes) below:</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift12.jpg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift12-800x449.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"449\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466012\" /></a></p>\n<p><a href=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift15.jpg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift15-800x448.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"448\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466013\" /></a></p>\n<p><a href=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift18.jpg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift18-800x449.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"449\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466014\" /></a></p>\n<p>Next, they compared the Olympus output to both the Sony and the Fuji GFX.</p>\n<p>Interestingly, the quality of the Olympus file came out <em>much</em> sharper if you process the files in Olympus&#8217; own Workspace software, as compared to using Photoshop. You can see a side-by-side below and there&#8217;s really no comparison: if you&#8217;re using the pixel shift mode on your Olympus camera, definitely use Workspace to stack the images.</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift26.jpg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift26-800x449.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"449\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466016\" /></a></p>\n<p>The rest of the comparisons were done using the Workspace version (obviously) in order to keep quality as high as possible.</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s the Olympus 4-image stack against the Sony with no image shift, and then the against the Sony&#8217;s 4-image stack mode:</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift28.jpg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift28-800x448.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"448\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466018\" /></a></p>\n<p><a href=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift27.jpg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift27-800x448.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"448\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466017\" /></a></p>\n<p>Finally, you can see the Olympus pixel shift image followed by the GFX all by itself below. For some reason, they didn&#8217;t show these side-by-side in the video:</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift31.jpg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift31-800x449.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"449\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466020\" /></a></p>\n<p><a href=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift35.jpg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/PixelShift35-800x449.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"449\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-466021\" /></a></p>\n<p>An interesting aside: Jay makes a good point at the very beginning of the video before jumping in. It&#8217;s worth reprinting in full just to keep these kinds of technical comparisons in perspective:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The reality of photography is: if it&#8217;s creative, and it communicates, and people will pay you for it, that&#8217;s commercial art. It doesn&#8217;t matter if you shot it with a shoebox, with a piece of tin, with a hole pocked in the front of it. It doesn&#8217;t matter.</p>\n<p>So these kinds of conversations are interesting. But the reality is that they are for tech heads.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Of course, there&#8217;s nothing wrong with being a &#8220;tech head&#8221; and enjoying the occasional pixel-peeping comparison, but it&#8217;s worth keeping Jay&#8217;s words in mind since sensor size comparisons tend to get people&#8217;s blood pressure into the danger zone.</p>\n<p>Anyway, to see this intriguing comparison for yourself and compare more side-by-side images of pixel shift vs medium format vs non pixel shift, check out the full video up top or head over to <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Ftheslantedlens.com%2F2020%2Fcan-pixel-shift-give-you-the-best-high-resolution-images%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">The Slanted Lens website</a> to read their full write-up.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><em><strong>Image credits</strong>: The plan was already brewing during peak photography for me; by 2016 the wheels were in motion and in 2017, our first model was released to much nail biting and eventually success. </p>\n<p>In the three years since our public debut, weâ€™ve released 16 models, been shortlisted for and won the industryâ€™s biggest award, and become both commercially viable and sought after. We wonâ€™t make the mistake of growing too fast and being unable to uphold the level of collector engagement we started off with; instead, weâ€™ll aim for a sustainable point that lets us have meaningful conversations with our buyers, make watches that continue to interest us personally and have the resources, time and mental overhead to make interesting images and drive engaging cars. </p>\n<p>Iâ€™ve come to realize that the spark required to keep oneâ€™s enthusiasm alive is maintained both by not fixating too much on one thing and being open to cross-disciplinary inspiration; itâ€™s hard to keep an open mind if you canâ€™t see beyond your immediate situation.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/50250156738_b3511237be_c.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"531\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-465619\" /></p>\n<p>Iâ€™m not ruling out another publicly shared/photographic project in the future, but right now I have no idea what form that might take â€“ or if it will happen at all. The curation thus remains simple and there is nothing to defend, apologize or make excuses for â€“ or be overly sensitive of an external opinion about.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/50250998022_d7d799a361_c.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"564\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-465620\" /></p>\n<p>I started off wanting to record my experiences. Iâ€™ll leave a clue: itâ€™s really about photographing <em>light</em> first, transients second, and everything else as a supporting actor. Light and timing transcend the subject from what it is most of the time, into what it could be.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/50198311372_d5b31bb2df_c.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"531\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-465621\" /></p>\n<p>Itâ€™s been an intense eight and a half years. Thank you to all of you for the support<sup>2</sup>, encouragement, challenges, and friendship â€“ itâ€™s time for me to start making pictures for myself again, and I hope you all continue to do so too. New comments on my site will be disabled from the end of September and I will no longer be replying, but the archive listings will be updated and the site itself will remain active for the foreseeable future â€“ producing it was a huge undertaking and thereâ€™s a lot of emotional attachment there. It only makes sense to leave it up as a resource â€“ perhaps inspiring some people, perhaps rewarding others with a kernel or two of insight. </p>\n<p>If it accomplishes that much â€“ Iâ€™ve achieved far more there than I set out to do.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><sup>1</sup> APSC Fuji 1010 Tiara, if you must know. style=\"max-width: 800px;\"><div class=\"fluid-iframe__inner\" style=\"padding-top:56.25%\"><iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/jrnG2Lrogio\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></div></div></p>\n<p>Here weâ€™re going to show you how to create minimalist landscape photography and give you plenty of examples, techniques and tips to get you inspired for your own shoot. Firstly, letâ€™s answer; what is minimalist photography? </p>\n<p>Minimalist photography is a form of photography that is distinguished by extreme simplicity. It focuses solely on the smallest number of objects and it is normally composed in a clean, clinical way with very little differences in the colours and tones of the image.</p>\n<p>In the example below, we use long exposure photography to create a minimalist effect of a lighthouse out at sea. </p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/minimalist_1-800x398.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"398\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465994\" /></p>\n<p>Using long exposures in landscape photography is a great way to get that minimalist look. In this shot, itâ€™s allowed the waves of the water to blend together to create this smooth effect. This eliminates the texture and tones of the water which further enhances the minimalist effect. </p>\n<p>To view exactly how this shot was taken and the equipment used, check out the video up top.</p>\n<h2>More Examples of Minimalist Landscape Photography</h2>\n<p>In the landscape shot below, the minimalist effect has been created by a clever use of composition and by removing the color from the scene. The shotâ€™s main focus is the rock and the majority of the image is taken up by the sky. The shot can be broken up into just 3 parts. Going from the bottom you have the line of water, the triangle of the rock, then a sky with only a graduation of grey. </p>\n<p>The image has been broken down to the minimal of objects, colors and tones, thus given a perfect example of minimalist landscape photography. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465995\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465995\" style=\"width: 533px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/adrian-5fTfCvbJWWA-unsplash-533x800.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"533\" height=\"800\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465995\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465995\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Photo by <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Faows.co%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Adrian</a>, CC0</figcaption></figure>\n<hr />\n<p>Here is another example of a long exposure landscape. Again, this effect has smoothed out the water and the color scheme of the shot is harmonious using only blues and purples with an accent color of orange. There is a small focal point within one-third of the frame which helps give the image a bit of interest. </p>\n<p>A calming example of a minimalist landscape photo. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465997\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465997\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/3-800x450.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465997\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465997\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Camera Settings &#8211; f/16 &#8211; ISO 100 &#8211; 35mm Focal length &#8211; 120 second</figcaption></figure>\n<hr />\n<p>Proving again that long exposures are a good tip for creating this effect, here with have a shot made up of very little shapes and tones. If you break it down, you have a triangle in the centre, flanked by the smooth toneless water and at the top of the image a rectangle of blank sky. </p>\n<p>As with the others, itâ€™s a shot showing very little color, tones and objects which is creating a lovely minimalist effect.  </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_465998\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465998\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/fabrice-villard-k87jn9fnYdY-unsplash-800x533.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" class=\"size-large wp-image-465998\" /><figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465998\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Photo by <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.enclosed.ch%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Fabrice Villard</a>, CC0<br /></figcaption></figure>\n<p>To learn a few of the basic techniques involved in capturing images like these, check out the video up top. And feel free to share your own tips for minimalist photography in the comments!</p>\n<hr />\n<p><em><strong>About the Author</strong>: Marc Newton is a photographer, educational speaker, author, and founder of <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.theschoolofphotography.com\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">The School of Photography</a>. 00:48:04","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","title":"Microsoftâ€™s New AI â€˜Authenticatorâ€™ Spots Manipulated Photos and Videos","link":"http://petapixel.com/?p=465594","description":"<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/confidence_Feat-800x420.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"420\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465627\" /></p>\n<p>Earlier today, Microsoft announced two new tools that will help identify manipulated photos and videos. The first is a metadata-based system, and the second is a &#8220;Video Authenticator&#8221; that will analyze photos and videos and provide a &#8220;confidence score&#8221; that tells you whether or not the media has been altered by AI.</p>\n<p>The metadata system that Microsoft talks about sounds similar to <a href=\"https://petapixel.com/2020/08/04/this-is-how-adobes-upcoming-photo-authenticity-system-will-work/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\">Adobe&#8217;s upcoming &#8220;Authenticity&#8221; system</a>: one program is used by the original creator to add certain tags to an image, and another checks those tags to tell you whether or not you&#8217;re looking at the original or a manipulated version. That seems pretty straight forward, and not terribly ground-breaking. </p>\n<p>What sounds far more interesting is the so-called &#8220;Microsoft Video Authenticator,&#8221; which is actually meant for both stills and video. According to Microsoft:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Video Authenticator can analyze a still photo or video to provide a percentage chance, or confidence score, that the media is artificially manipulated. In the case of a video, it can provide this percentage in real-time on each frame as the video plays. It works by detecting the blending boundary of the deepfake and subtle fading or greyscale elements that might not be detectable by the human eye.</p></blockquote>\n<p>You can see the system in action, frame-by-frame, in the GIF below:</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/Disinf-GIF.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-465614\" /></p>\n<p>The tech was designed to fight <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FDeepfake\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">deepfakes</a>: manipulated photos and videos that are created by deep-learning algorithms (hence: <em>deep</em> fake). These manipulated filesâ€”which are often used to make it seem like a prominent celebrity or political figure said or did something they did not say or doâ€”are becoming increasingly problematic since the algorithms are always learning, creating more-and-more convincing and hard-to-detect fakes. </p>\n<p>This is what Video Authenticator is trying to defend against, and it was trained using the latest-and-greatest datasets for deefake detection.</p>\n<p>Since this, itself, is an AI-powered &#8220;deep learning&#8221; based system, it won&#8217;t be released broadly to the public, where bad actors could potentially train their algorithms against it. The Microsoft Video Authenticator will instead be available through a partnership with the AI Foundationâ€™s <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Frd2020.org%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Reality Defender 2020</a> (RD2020) initiative, and anyone who is interested in learning more or getting access to the tech will need to reach out to RD2020 <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Frd2020.org%2F%23involved\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">here</a>.</p>\n<p>(via <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.engadget.com%2Fmicrosoft-misinformation-deepfake-tools-165700270.html\" 00:48:04","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","title":"Panasonic Unveils the S5: A Compact Full-Frame Camera for Hybrid Shooters","link":"http://petapixel.com/?p=465561","description":"<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/s5_feat-800x420.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"420\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465569\" /></p>\n<p>Panasonic has just unveiled the much-rumored and heavily leaked <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.adorama.com%2Fpcs5.html%3Fkbid%3D67085\" rel=\"norewrite follow external noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Lumix S5</a>: a compact, entry(ish)-level full-frame mirrorless camera that packs a lot of impressive video and stills features into a more compact and affordable L-mount body.</p>\n<p>A lot of the &#8220;core&#8221; features of the Panasonic S5 are similar to <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.adorama.com%2Fpcs1.html%3Fkbid%3D67085\" rel=\"norewrite follow external noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">the more expensive S1</a>: it uses the same 24MP BSI CMOS sensor, can shoot 96MP photos in high-res multi-shot mode, and boasts 5-axis in-body image stabilization (IBIS) with up to 6.5 stops of shake reduction when you use a compatible lens. </p>\n<p>The Lumix S5 just packs all of this into a more compact body that uses dual SD card slots (one UHS-II and one UHS-I) instead of SD and CFExpress, a lower resolution LCD screen (1.84M dots) and EVF (2.36M dots), and no top-mounted LCD screen.</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/s5_9-800x500.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"500\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465576\" /></p>\n<p>In terms of improvements, Panasonic has focused primarily on autofocus performance, low-light performance, and video features. </p>\n<p>The AF system has been re-vamped and updated with the latest deep-learning technology to improve speed and precision, and the company&#8217;s Depth from Defocus (DFD) system used for continuous AF has been improved as well (which hopefully means less &#8220;wobble&#8221; in video).</p>\n<p>In terms of low-light shooting, the Lumix S5 features Dual Native ISO for cleaner performance at high ISO when shooting either stills or video. In V-Log, your native ISOs are 640 and 4000, but you can crank the ISO up to a (probably unusable) 51,200, just like you can on the S1.</p>\n<p>Finally, when it comes to video features, the S5 has a lot on offer with even more to come via firmware update. At launch, you&#8217;ll be able to shoot 4K/60p video at up to 10-bit 4:2:0 with an APS-C crop, or 4K 30p/24p video at up to 10-bit 4:2:2 using the full sensor width. If you slap an external recorder on it, you can output 4K/60p 10-bit 4:2:2 footage over HDMI no problem. And yes, you can also output RAW video when using an Atomos Ninja V.</p>\n<p>In that sense, you can think of the Lumix S5 as a more balanced, lighter, and <em>much cheaper</em> little brother to the video-centric <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.adorama.com%2Fpcs1h.html%3Fkbid%3D67085\" rel=\"norewrite follow external noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Panasonic S1H</a>&#8230; or maybe a full-frame GH5.</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s a closer look at the new camera:</p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/s5-800x500.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"500\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465579\" /></p>\n<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/s5_1-800x500.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"500\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465570\" /></p>\n<p><img hands-on from <a starting today for <a Shipping is expected to start by mid-September, and if you&#8217;re in the US, every pre-order that&#8217;s submitted before September 30th will receive a free Sigma 45mm f/2.8 DG DN lens.</p>\n<p>At that price it&#8217;s definitely Panasonic&#8217;s S-series entry-level camera, at least for now, though the &#8220;entry level&#8221; moniker doesn&#8217;t <em>quite</em> fit since the S5 is definitely in a different league than competitors like the <a dn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn94@2020_2/2020/09/04/16-48-12-311_6828c1a7e29daf99.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/PetaPixel?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn92@2020_1/2020/09/04/16-48-17-572_701e8443590d36d5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/PetaPixel?i=fRFlvKt1_Pw:6zGrAMTDcg4:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn23@2020_2/2020/09/04/16-48-15-061_6e822b0a6d382762.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/PetaPixel?i=fRFlvKt1_Pw:6zGrAMTDcg4:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn55@2020_3/2020/09/04/16-48-16-593_e5ce40e3feb64d8b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/PetaPixel?i=fRFlvKt1_Pw:6zGrAMTDcg4:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn23@2020_6/2020/09/04/16-48-16-487_5e247013f39bea23.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/PetaPixel/~4/fRFlvKt1_Pw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn25@2020_6/2020/09/04/16-48-12-254_aafbd33c99bfa0c3.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599238084516},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 00:48:04","title":"Photographing VP Joe Biden in His â€˜Battle for the Soul of Americaâ€™","link":"http://petapixel.com/?p=465482","description":"<p><img src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/bidenbookcover-751x800.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"751\" height=\"800\" class=\"aligncenter size-large wp-image-465822\" /></p> \n<p>With the 2020 election looming large on the horizon, former Vice President Joe Biden’s official White House photographer <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.davidlienemann.com%2Findex\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">David Lienemann</a> is stepping forward to show Americans the real “regular Joe,” as he fondly calls the VP.</p> \n<p>Lienemann’s 256-page hardcover <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2FBiden-Obama-Years-Battle-America%2Fdp%2F0316593230%2Fref%3Dsr_1_1%3Fcrid%3D38BMRJO23SV4K%26dchild%3D1%26keywords%3Ddavid%2Blienemann%26qid%3D1598135382%26sprefix%3Ddavid%2Blien%252Caps%252C152%26sr%3D8-1\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\"><em>Biden: The Obama Years and the Battle for the Soul of America</em></a> is due to be published by Voracious on September 8th. </p> \n<p>Lienemann presents the many faces of Joe, from taking the field for the Baltimore Orioles season opener with granddaughters Finnegan and Maisy to commemorating the Civil Rights movement with the late Congressman John Lewis in Selma to officiating a same-sex marriage of White House staffers to his official duties as former President Obama’s second in command.</p> \n<p>“Looking back at David’s photographs, I am filled with deep pride,” writes Dr. Jill Biden in the foreword. “He captured it all: the hours of work, the questions and negotiations, the emotions that spanned from such incredible highs to such heartbreaking lows, every hard-fought battleâ€¦I know the hope I see in David’s pictures is not gone. It is alive, and its power will continue to transform our nation for the betterâ€¦These photographs invigorate me for the challenge ahead, and I hope they do the same for you.”</p> \n<p>We sat down with Lienemann, as he cradled his 16-month daughter Millie in their New Mexico home, to hear his story of the eight years he spent in the White House with the VP and what he wants Americans to see.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465502\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465502\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465502\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/P101515LJ-0097.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465502\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  David Lienemann (kneeling) photographs President Barack Obama delivering a statement on Afghanistan, in the Roosevelt Room of the White House, Oct. 15, 2015. Vice President Joe Biden, Defense Secretary Ashton Carter and Gen. Joseph F. Dunford, Jr., Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff, stand with the President. (Official White House Photo by Lawrence Jackson)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>Phil Mistry: How did the book project come about?</strong></p> \n<p>David Lienemann: The book project came about when a former White House coworker of mine suggested that I should work on a book shortly after Joe Biden crossed the delegate threshold in the democratic primary. I reached out to my former boss <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2FObama-Intimate-Portrait-Pete-Souza%2Fdp%2F0316512583%2Fref%3Dsr_1_2%3Fdchild%3D1%26keywords%3Dpete%2Bsouza%26qid%3D1598126543%26sr%3D8-2\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Pete Souza</a> who was the director of the Photo Office, who connected me with his agent David Black. I ended up working with Pete’s publisher as well, Michael Szczerban at <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hachettebookgroup.com%2Ftitles%2Fdavid-lienemann%2Fbiden%2F9780316593212%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Voracious</a>.</p> \n<p><strong>Tell us about the photo selection process?</strong></p> \n<p>Sure. It’s obviously challenging to narrow down from hundreds of thousands of photos to just a couple of hundred images to try to tell the story of eight years. I really wanted to give readers a sense of who Joe Biden is. A family man, a man of faith, who always wanted to know how government policies would affect the working-class people in the neighborhood where he grew up. </p> \n<p>The book encompasses a wide variety of photographs, from the early days of the Obama Biden Administration to the first trip to Iraq as VP, where he swore in new US Citizens in a 4<sup>th</sup> of July Ceremony meeting with wounded warriors and grieving families who lost loved ones to gun violence. The highs and lows of the administration.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465493\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465493\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465493\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20120907-124055.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465493\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden delivers remarks at a campaign event at the Strawbery Banke Museum in Portsmouth, New Hampshire, Sept. 7, 2012. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>How did the title “Battle for the Soul of America” come about?</strong></p> \n<p>I believe it was a bit of a play on the campaign’s slogan, “Battle for the Soul of the Nation.” There was a lot of workshopping of how to acknowledge that it was both a look back at Joe Biden’s eight years as Barack Obama’s Vice President, and also a look forward at a possible Joe Biden presidency.</p> \n<p><strong>Which is your favorite image in the book? </strong></p> \n<p>Favorite image in the book is probably an easier question than favorite image. There are just so many to choose from! But, in the book, my favorite image is of Delaware Attorney General Beau Biden, the Vice President’s oldest son, and they’re standing backstage at the 2012 Democratic National Convention with Dr. Jill Biden waiting to go on stage. Amidst all the cheering and the music and thousands of people packed into an arena in Charlotte, Beau is quietly leaning over to straighten his father’s tie. There’s something really personal and kind about the moment.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465492\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465492\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465492\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20120906-211259.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465492\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden, Dr. Jill Biden, and Beau Biden hold backstage as Dr. Biden is introduced at the Democratic National Convention, at Time Warner Arena in Charlotte, North Carolina, September 6, 2012. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>If you have shot multiple images of a situation, do the not-so-good ones ever get deleted, or is each and every one saved to the archive?</strong></p> \n<p>All of the images we took are archived. Photos are covered under the <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.archives.gov%2Fpresidential-libraries%2Flaws%2F1978-act.html\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Presidential Records Act,</a> which requires they be saved and transferred to the <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.archives.gov%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">National Archives</a> at the end of the administration.</p> \n<p><strong>So, if an image is out of focus, is it still archived?</strong></p> \n<p>Yes, out of focus, blurry, I have some really terrible photos in the archives.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465500\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465500\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465500\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20170112-160600.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465500\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  President Barack Obama awards the Presidential Medal of Freedom with Distinction to Vice President Joe Biden during a tribute in the State Dining Room of the White House, Jan. 12, 2017. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>Did you shoot any photos at the White House with your cell phone? Have any gone on the record?</strong></p> \n<p>I took a couple of photos on my iPhone for work, and they are in the Archives, yes. I didn’t actively use it to shoot with because the quality of the files didn’t really match up with the quality of DSLR files at the time.</p> \n<p><strong>Are you trying to be invisible while you are at important meetings?</strong></p> \n<p>Always! Which doesn’t mean I never tripped over something while moving around the room. I tried to use quiet cameras, avoided flash whenever possible, and just tried to blend in, to not distract or take away from what was going on.</p> \n<p><strong>How challenging is this job to work in the White House?</strong></p> \n<p>I talk about it a little bit in the introduction to the book. It’s a really unique job and an incredible opportunity as well. You alluded to this earlier, about trying to be invisible while you’re in the room taking photos. You want to be there to capture every moment because something that seems mundane one day might turn out to be an immensely meaningful moment later on. </p> \n<p>At the same time, the more photographs you take, the more there is to sift through, and unfortunately, you can only work so many hours in a day. It also can be a bit of a 24-7 job sometimes. I worked a lot of holidays and missed a lot of time with my family. I also met my now wife at an event with the Vice President.</p> \n<p><strong>How much did you travel with the VP?</strong></p> \n<p>Honestly, not sure on the mileage as they tracked his mileage, and I missed a few trips with him. [I] went on a couple of trips with Dr. [Jill] Biden, safe to say, over a million miles though. Forty-seven states and sixty-four countries, I had to go back and count them all up to make sure the numbers were correct.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465499\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465499\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465499\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20160604-141859.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465499\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden engages in a super soaker battle during the 2016 Biden Beach Boardwalk Bash held at the Naval Observatory Residence in Washington, D.C., June 4, 2016. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>How many images did you shoot in the eight years?</strong></p> \n<p>Just under a million images, we tried to do a quick count in the last week of the administration, but it was a real whirlwind of packing up my office, trying to respond to as many emails as I could, and send as many photos out as possible.</p> \n<p><strong>So, can anybody see the complete archive of VP photos that you took?</strong></p> \n<p>I don’t believe so. I’m not completely up to speed on how the National Archives handle records, but I think they become more public over time, but I think it’s still handled, to some extent, by request.</p> \n<p><strong>Do you shoot JPEG or RAW?</strong></p> \n<p>Actually, I shoot both. The first couple of years, cameras only had a single card slot. We archived the RAW files, and the JPEGs were just there in case something went wrong with the card since they were slightly easier to recover with file recovery software. In the later years, when cameras had dual slots, RAW files went on one card and JPEGs to a second card that just lived in the cameraâ€¦ again as sort of a redundancy in case of card failure.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465497\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465497\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465497\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20160401-151525.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465497\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden drives his restored 1967 Corvette with Jay Leno during a taping of “Jay Leno’s Garage” at the USSS training facility in Laurel, Maryland, April 1, 2016. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>Did you edit the photos? What was your software of choice?</strong></p> \n<p>Editing in the sense of choosing photographs, I used <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fhome.camerabits.com%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Photo Mechanic</a> to browse images and tag them. I know a lot of folks like <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.adobe.com%2Fproducts%2Fphotoshop-lightroom.html%3Fsdid%3DKKTJE%26mv%3Dsearch%26ef_id%3DCj0KCQjwhIP6BRCMARIsALu9LfnOOtbL8uecmR6xG-1l8q727mTIRdwNxAAhXExk4DDRUaXtqlZkxc0aAvp4EALw_wcB%3AG%3As%26s_kwcid%3DAL%213085%213%21442365416288%21e%21%21g%21%21lightroom%26gclid%3DCj0KCQjwhIP6BRCMARIsALu9LfnOOtbL8uecmR6xG-1l8q727mTIRdwNxAAhXExk4DDRUaXtqlZkxc0aAvp4EALw_wcB\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Lightroom</a> for this, and I’ve looked at it but just never have felt as comfortable with it. Editing actual images, yes, in the traditional journalism sense of cropping, adjusting exposure, and trying to achieve an accurate color representation of a room. But not editing in the sense of adding or removing people from the room.</p> \n<p><strong>What is your deadline for delivery?</strong></p> \n<p>Depends, photos for social media, the <a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.whitehouse.gov%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">White House Website</a>, or release to the media were prioritized and happened as quickly as was possible. Posed photos of folks from a photo line after an event, we tried to get out as quickly as possible, but the process wasn’t perfect. I will note that I was helped with this by Jordan Brooks early in the Administration and Chris Mackler in the later years.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465498\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465498\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465498\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20160402-203533.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465498\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden greets Syracuse fans between games at the Final Four at NRG Stadium in Houston, Texas, April 2, 2016. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>Would you ever drastically crop, like making a horizontal frame into a vertical photo?</strong></p> \n<p>Sure. We had something called Jumbos. They were large photos in the West Wing of the White House that were periodically changed out. I had one vertical jumbo frame at the end of the hallway, and sometimes I’d shot plenty of verticals and had no problems filling it, and sometimes we were scrambling to try to find something that would crop nicely from a horizontal.</p> \n<p><strong>Is it OK to crop out unimportant people from the frame?</strong></p> \n<p>I think I cropped more because I hadn’t shot the image the way I wanted, whether the camera was tilted slightly, or I hadn’t used a long enough lens, couldn’t get close enough to achieve the image I was trying to create to tell the story.</p> \n<p><strong>How do you win the trust of the important people you work within the White House?</strong></p> \n<p>That’s an interesting question I thought about when I was writing for the book, and I’ve talked to photo students about before. There’s obviously the background check side of working there where the government does a deep dive into your background to make sure you aren’t a spy. But building trust with the Vice President and Cabinet members takes time, being respectful and obviously not sharing things that are said behind closed doors or posting on social media.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465495\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465495\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465495\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20130303-160029.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465495\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden marches across the Edmund Pettus Bridge with Congresswoman Terri Sewell and Congressman John Lewis, during the 48th annual Bridge Crossing Ceremony in Selma, Alabama, March 3, 2013. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>Did you shoot with zooms or primes? Which ones?</strong></p> \n<p>I used both primes and zooms. When I was in the West Wing or most of the time on the road, I had a 24-70 on one camera body, it just covers so much range for the kind of photos I was making given the access I had. My second camera sometimes had a 70-200, 35, or 85mm lens depending on what was happening. In rare occasions, I’d use something much longer or wider, but the bulk of my photographs were captured on a 24-70mm.</p> \n<p><strong>If you had to use only one lens on a foreign trip, which would it be?</strong></p> \n<p>Foreign travel at the White House? Probably that 24-70, 2.8. In most countries, they had arranged access with my counterpart, and so I wasn’t stuck on a riser 100 feet away. Foreign travel for me as a private citizen? I shoot an awful lot with a 35mm lens now, and then for that second lens, something in the super-telephoto range like a 100-400mm.</p> \n<p>Sorry for the delay. The baby came in to see what I was up to.</p> \n<p><strong>What is the baby’s name? How old?</strong></p> \n<p>Her name is Millie. She’s 16 months.</p> \n<p>Don’t ask how many photos I’ve taken of her, I have no idea, but I’m sure it’s a ridiculous number.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465491\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465491\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465491\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20110701-135348.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465491\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden talks with Nate Tamarin, Shailagh Murray, Fran Person, Mike Donilon and Matt Teper about his speech to the International Brotherhood of Teamsters National Convention, aboard Air Force Two, en route to Las Vegas, Nevada, July 1, 2011. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>It will quickly climb to over a million!</strong></p> \n<p><strong>Which cameras did you shoot with?</strong></p> \n<p>At the White House, the photo office used Canon. I also dabbled with Leica, Nikon, and in the last year of the administration, a Fuji X-Pro2, which I loved as a digital rangefinder, plus weight/size and silent shooting. Since the end of the administration, I’ve used both Fuji and Sony cameras.</p> \n<p><strong>Was the sound of the shutter on the Canon DSLR distracting to Joe?</strong></p> \n<p>I honestly don’t think he was. We used [Canon] 5D cameras, which are pretty quiet, and they are silent. If you’re trying to take photos during a TV interview, you want to be silent. If he’s consoling someone who lost their child or their parent or spouse, you want to not distract from that moment.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465496\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465496\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465496\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20130727-140923.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465496\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden talks with Commander Timothy Wilke, on board the Littoral Combat Ship U.S.S. Freedom during a tactical team demonstration, from the Waterborne Mission Zone on board the U.S.S. Freedom, at Changi Navy Base, in Singapore, July 27, 2013. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>Did you use flash where there was no risk of disturbing anybody, like in larger spaces?</strong></p> \n<p>I used flash for photo lines after an event, which were often poorly lit. And I’d occasionally use it outside for photos if the lighting really required it. But I’m not much of a flash photographer. I’ve always tried to work with available light as much as possible.</p> \n<p><strong>If both Obama and Biden were present, then were both Pete [Souza] and you shooting simultaneously?</strong></p> \n<p>I’m not sure I understand the question. Do you mean in the previous administration when they were together?</p> \n<p><strong>That is correct when they were making joint appearances.</strong></p> \n<p>Got it. So, when they were in the Oval Office, Pete covered it, if they were doing an event in the Rose Garden or an event in Pennsylvania or Ohio, then we were both there.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465489\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465489\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465489\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20100123-112256.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465489\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden visits with 4-2 Stryker Troops at Camp Victory, Baghdad, Iraq, January 23, 2010. (White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>Unlike Obama’s official photographer Pete Souza, who had a staff of shooters, you only got backing under special circumstances. When did that happen?</strong></p> \n<p>So, we all worked in the same office and helped each other out when possible. Chuck Kennedy, Lawrence Jackson, and Amanda Lucidon all covered for me periodically, whether I was trying to take a couple of days off to get away, or if I was traveling with Dr. [Jill] Biden to visit a refugee camp in Kenya.</p> \n<p><strong>Are you allowed to keep the photos from the archive on your personal computer?</strong></p> \n<p>I did some work for the Bidens after the administration, so I have some of the photos from my time at the White House.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465494\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465494\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465494\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20130121-114642.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"534\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465494\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Supreme Court Associate Justice Sonia Sotomayor administers the oath of office to Vice President Joe Biden, who stands with Dr. Jill Biden, Beau Biden, Ashley Biden and Hunter Biden, during the inaugural swearing-in ceremony at the U.S. Capitol in Washington, D.C., Jan. 21, 2013. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>Can you tell us about the shooting of the official portrait? How long did the session last? </strong></p> \n<p>From setup to teardown, probably 30 minutes? I’d been working on another idea with my colleague Chuck Kennedy, so we’d set up some lights and dialed in a concept a little bit. Then the VP asked if we could try a photo in front of his desk at the end of the day, so while he went to his last meeting of the day with President Obama, I set up a light with a large poster board sized bounce card. Chuck stood in for a couple of frames to make sure everything looked good, and we moved the computer, phone, etc. off the VP’s desk.</p> \n<p><strong>Did you photograph Biden at his residence as well as the White House?</strong></p> \n<p>Sure, he held meetings there occasionally, hosted foreign leaders for meals, the Bidens hosted receptions there, holiday parties.</p> \n<p><strong>How did you transition from Cornell College with a BA in Economics and Business in 2005 to photojournalism?</strong></p> \n<p>I studied economics and business at Cornell College, but realized in my junior year that I wasn’t sure that Excel spreadsheets and crunching numbers was how I wanted to spend my time after graduation. I’d always really liked photography. I’d been freelancing for the local weekly paper and had spent some time job shadowing at the Cedar Rapids<em> Gazette,</em> which covered eastern Iowa. I was really fortunate to get a string of newspaper internships after college, which gave me a tremendous amount of experience in photography. Going to college in Iowa also meant that I was exposed to a lot of politicians and political activity during the runup to the Iowa caucus.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465490\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465490\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465490\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20110211-092726.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465490\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden boards Air Force 2 at Joint Base Andrews, Maryland February 11, 2011. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>How did you end up getting picked for this job?</strong></p> \n<p>I first photographed Joe Biden, along with the other 15 candidates during 2007 in the lead up to the Iowa Caucus. I saw and was inspired by his ability to connect with Americans on the campaign trail as a “regular Joe.” He always took the time to talk to everyone in the room.</p> \n<p>So, when he was picked as the VP nominee, I started reaching out to everyone I knew in his office to see if I could join the campaign as his photographer. And when he got sworn in as Vice President, I moved to Washington and joined the photo office about six weeks later.</p> \n<p><strong>What was it like for a 24-year-old, when you started at the White House?</strong></p> \n<p>It was an incredible experience. I’d worked as a freelance photographer covering the campaign in 2007, so I covered then-Senator Biden and Senator Obama and of all the other candidates that were running in 2007-08. But as you alluded to, going from being a journalist to a 24-year-old White House photographer, traveling with the Vice President of the United States all over the country and all over the world. It was a really, incredible opportunity to get to serve in the Obama Biden administration.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465503\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465503\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465503\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/V110612DL-1118.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465503\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  President Barack Obama, First Lady Michelle Obama,Vice President Joe Biden and Dr. Jill Biden wave to the crowd as confetti rains down, following the Presidentâ€™s election night remarks at McCormick Place in Chicago, Illinois, Nov. 6, 2012. (Official White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>Are you going to be covering the Biden campaign?</strong></p> \n<p>I helped photograph the big kickoff rally in Philadelphia last year and covered a few other events along the way. I’m not sure, given the COVID-19 situation, what or how much in-person campaigning will happen this fall, but I’m obviously willing to help as much as possible.</p> \n<p><strong>If Joe becomes President, do you pack your bags for another eight years? That would end up being the longest stint for any photographer at the White House.</strong></p> \n<p>I’m not positive, but I believe my old boss Pete Souza worked for most of President Reagan’s two terms as well as all eight years of the Obama administration.</p> \n<p>That said, right now I’m focused on sharing with the American people who the Joe Biden I got to know during my eight years at the White House is, and trying my best to help him get elected… I don’t have any plans for January.</p> \n<p><strong>What do you shoot for fun?</strong></p> \n<p>I love taking photos of the outdoors, hiking, and camping. I’ve recently had an older camera converted to black &amp; white infrared that I’ve been sort of playing around with a little bit.</p> \n<figure id=\"attachment_465488\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-465488\" style=\"width: 800px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\">\n <img class=\"size-full wp-image-465488\" src=\"http://petapixel.com/assets/uploads/2020/09/20090522-021024.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"800\" height=\"533\" />\n <figcaption id=\"caption-attachment-465488\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">\n  Vice President Joe Biden talks to National Security Advisor Tony Blinken as he lands at Pristina Airport in Kosovo, Friday, May 22, 2009. (White House Photo by David Lienemann)\n </figcaption>\n</figure> \n<p><strong>What advice would you have for aspiring photographers who want to be a White House photographer?</strong></p> \n<p>I think having a relevant portfolio of images is helpful. I’d certainly cover sports and breaking news and other things. I had spent a year photographing politics before I got the job.</p> \n<p>I also think being professional, able to dress well and read the room are also hugely important skills, some of which I was better at than others when I started working there.</p> \n<hr /> \n<p><em>You can find more of David Lienemann’s work on his<a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.davidlienemann.com%2Findex\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\">Â&nbsp;<strong>website</strong></a> andÂ&nbsp;<a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.instagram.com%2Fdccl%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\"><strong>Instagram,</strong></a> where he is posting a photo a day, some from the book, up until the election.</em></p> \n<hr /> \n<p><em><strong>About the author</strong>: Phil Mistry is a photographer and teacher based in Atlanta, GA. He started one of the first digital camera classes in New York City at </em><a href=\"http://apicdn.viglink.com/api/click?format=go&amp;key=dae5b94bb21a32cc7c141a041d18f05b&amp;loc=https%3A%2F%2Fpetapixel.com%2Ffeed%2F&amp;out=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.icp.org%2F\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"follow external noopener noreferrer\"><em>The International Center of Photography</em></a><em>Â&nbsp;in the 90s. He was the director and teacher for Sony/Popular Photography magazine’s Digital Days Workshops. You can reach him via emailÂ&nbsp;</em><a href=\"mailto:philmistry2@gmail.com\"><em>here</em></a><em>.</em></p> \n<hr /> \n<p><strong><em>Image credits:</em></strong><em>Â&nbsp; Little Brown &amp; Co. and David Lienemann and used with permission.
